    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/991817373?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rey" href="/user/show/32785524-rey">Rey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer991817373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12956382234310937594">When I was 8 I saw a movie my parents rented. The only part of the movie I remembered was the fact that it was a Vampire movie, and saw a guy walking towards his sister all scary, she screamed and he stopped and said "sorry, I was pretending to be a vampire" I couldn't remember what movie it was, but that one Scene stayed stuck in my head for the next 5 years. Just last year I was scrolling through my TV guide on the Syfy channel to see what time the new season of Being Human was gonna start up </span>
  <span id="freeText12956382234310937594" style="display:none">When I was 8 I saw a movie my parents rented. The only part of the movie I remembered was the fact that it was a Vampire movie, and saw a guy walking towards his sister all scary, she screamed and he stopped and said "sorry, I was pretending to be a vampire" I couldn't remember what movie it was, but that one Scene stayed stuck in my head for the next 5 years. Just last year I was scrolling through my TV guide on the Syfy channel to see what time the new season of Being Human was gonna start up again. As I was scrolling through what was gonna play until night time, I came across Cirque Du Freak: The Vampire Assistant. I passed it, but then went back. I had priorly found that movie I remembered from when I was 8 and knew the title was some weird name in a different language. That's how I recognized he name. Long story short, I recorded the<br />Movie, watched it, asked my friends if they saw it, and one if them said she read the books and have yet to seem the movie. <br /><br />Since I like to read the books and compare them to it's movie, I found my local library and started to read all 12 books. I have to say that the series is looong, but somehow Darren Shan managed to keep it interesting the whole way through. He kept old vampire myths in the book, and also added some other really cool monsters that just fit in the story so well. He also did an excellent job with the story plot, even though I wish he hadn't jumped months and years ahead I between books. It's an excellent read, all the characters have their own personalities and Darren Shan did a marvelous Job at showing his readers how the world of Darren Shan is. <br /><br />To those who think the author is selfish for naming the main character after himself, read the prologue of the first book, read all of the books, and in one if the books, you'll be sitting there with your mouth wide open saying "oh, aaahhh. I get it now." And if your like me, you'll be recalling back through out the series, look for the clues, Daren Shan gives you so many through out all 12 books. <br /><br />Highly recommended, for teens and young adults.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12956382234310937594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9494102133058449008">When I was 23 and a 15 year old brother of a friend handed me this series and said I should read it, I mostly started reading it just to amuse him. How little did I know I would get completely sucked into this crazy world. I love the way Darren Shan writes. It's full of twists and turns and I became very attached to the characters.   <span id="freeText9494102133058449008" style="display:none">When I was 23 and a 15 year old brother of a friend handed me this series and said I should read it, I mostly started reading it just to amuse him. How little did I know I would get completely sucked into this crazy world. I love the way Darren Shan writes. It's full of twists and turns and I became very attached to the characters. There were several times that I had to stop, put the book down, and walk away just to absorb the twist that had just happened. The whole series was full of great twists and turns and I never really knew what was about to come next. The way the different types of vampires and the societies were portrayed was also a kind of different I enjoyed. I highly recommend this series. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2110494898" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1436012303257937002">These books provided some stiff competition for J.K Rowling in my house, though both hold a very dear place in my teenage heart. I loved this saga, which in my opinion only gets better as the stories progress. The reader is truly taken on a journey with Darren as the narrative develops and becomes more intricate. They are evidence of some fantastic storytelling, which kept me turning pages well after my bed time and going right back to the start to relive it once again!<br/><br/>I still look back on these</span>
  <span id="freeText1436012303257937002" style="display:none">These books provided some stiff competition for J.K Rowling in my house, though both hold a very dear place in my teenage heart. I loved this saga, which in my opinion only gets better as the stories progress. The reader is truly taken on a journey with Darren as the narrative develops and becomes more intricate. They are evidence of some fantastic storytelling, which kept me turning pages well after my bed time and going right back to the start to relive it once again!<br /><br />I still look back on these with fondness, and I know were I to pick these up once again as a adult, they would be just as compelling and impressive to me now as they were then. Its a shame the film was such a disappointment, as had it been done to a better standard I think the story really would have taken off. I would recommend these to anyone who loves to submerge themselves in the fantasy/horror genre, with the added fun of some teenage angst.</span>

I appreciate when an author can write themselves into a corner and pull off a great ending to a series that leaves the reader thinking about it after finishing it. The series had some great characters, Vancha's my fave, and dark moments for a YA series. I probably won't read the prequels or any other novels by the author, but I am glad that I finished this series from my adolescence. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8299779183206247082">I remember this series being one of the first vampire books I read (along with Twilight) when I really started getting into reading. I devoured the first book in a day. Up to this day, the plot still feels fresh, unique, and exciting. Maybe it's not the vampire book people are used to with the sensual characters and dark romances, but The Saga of Darren Shan is definitely worth a look if you're up for a different kind of adventure. </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LF1nYjWidjytqZWW/cpUGyKDofsnTsz6pwxA6I+VuNtD19P7bpV7maXF0RDeM1QUu9T4BqPs5ta8dDjDMvfrRA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mPe2mLfKTe9rZxCU7BqKsH9rG8jdLiYZEfbRsyYFMqn3fQIB7P1ASmMLVBLP44q/5jxCNVmMDDUKjqmYm2dhNg==')})
  }
//]]>

  <span id="freeText1274846160981661392" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>
